Local News

Arbitration Results of the Pawn Industry Labor Strike Yesterday 105

All Employees Receive Graded Pay Raises

Both Parties Sign Agreement for Immediate Resumption of Work Today

Over Two Hundred Workers Petitioned the Party Headquarters Together

After the pawn industry workers' strike entered its fourth day, representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters' Public Training Committee and the Social Affairs Bureau convened labor and management representatives yesterday afternoon at the Party Headquarters for mediation. The result was that all pawn industry employees were divided into three grades (A, B, and C) and received universal pay raises. The management also recognized the workers' union's right to represent its members. Both parties signed an agreement, and the striking workers are scheduled to fully resume work today. During the mediation, over two hundred workers marched to the Party Headquarters to petition. On their way, passing Wansheng Bridge in Ximen, they saw that Cuiyuan Pawnshop was open for business. The crowd knocked down its signboard and urged it to close. Yesterday, over one hundred labor unions across the city held a meeting to discuss providing assistance to the three workers who were previously sentenced by the court. They decided to bail them out today and file an appeal. The details of each situation are recorded below:

Mediation Situation

Attending Representatives: Yesterday afternoon at 1 p.m., labor and management representatives from the pawn industry, following the instructions of the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau, each sent responsible representatives to the Public Training Committee of the Party Headquarters to await mediation. The attendees included: (A) From the Municipal Party Headquarters' Public Training Committee: Tao Baichuan (representative for mediation), from the Social Affairs Bureau: Guo Yongxi (representative for mediation), Shi Shaohua (recorder). (B) From the labor side: Jin Futian, Cheng Zijun, Wang Ganchen, and Cheng Xingzhu (responsible representatives); Li Fulin and Hu Jinzhang were present as observers. (C) From the management side: Cheng Rufu, Yu Shaoqing, Shen Fuzhi, Wu Jiemei, Mu Jingshan, and Yu Langxi (responsible representatives). They were seated separately in the east side of the reception room on the ground floor of the Municipal Party Headquarters.

Chairman's Report: After the labor and management representatives were assembled, Tao Baichuan from the Public Training Committee and Guo Yongxi from the Social Affairs Bureau, acting as chairmen, began with a report from Tao Baichuan. He stated that all representatives present were expected to be fully responsible representatives. This dispute in the pawn industry originally fell within the scope of mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau. However, because worker organizations and employee groups have similar natures, the Labor-Management Dispute Resolution Law was not applicable for mediation or arbitration. Therefore, the Social Affairs Bureau had no legal basis for mediation, and the Party Headquarters convened both parties to discuss solutions on the twelfth of this month, in order to prevent the dispute from escalating. On that day, the three management representatives believed that the matter was important and needed to wait until after the general meeting of all members of the trade association on the fifteenth before proceeding with negotiations. The Party Headquarters thought this approach was reasonable, so it rescheduled the formal mediation for the seventeenth. Unexpectedly, the labor representatives arrived on the seventeenth and waited from 1 p.m. to 4 p.m., but the management representatives did not appear, making mediation impossible. This led to the strike on the eighteenth. It can be said that this strike by pawn industry workers was entirely caused by the issue of revising the contract. If the management representatives had come to mediate on the twelfth or seventeenth, the strike would not have occurred. The responsibility for this is very clear and should be borne by the management. Today, both parties are here, and it is hoped that everyone will openly and honestly discuss amending the contract so that the turmoil can be calmed down as soon as possible, etc. After the Chairman's report, the labor representative Wang Ganchen stood up and said that the management representative Yu Langxi was an outsider and had no right to attend. The chairman ordered him to stop speaking.

Amended Conditions: After discussions by both parties, the mediation was completed at 8 p.m., and the formal agreement was signed. The striking workers, under the order of the workers' union, will uniformly resume work starting this morning. The amended conditions are copied below: Agreement between the Shanghai Pawn Industry Association, the Special District Pawn Industry Association, and the Pawn Industry Workers' Union of Shanghai: Article 1 (Recognition): The Shanghai Pawn Industry Association and the Special District Pawn Industry Association recognize the right of the Pawn Industry Workers' Union to represent its members who have joined the union. Article 2 (Salary): Each pawn industry employee's monthly salary will be increased by 1.5 yuan for those earning 15 yuan or more, 3.5 yuan for those earning 10 yuan or more, and 5.5 yuan for those earning less than 10 yuan. Counter clerks will receive a double salary in December, uniformly at 10 yuan per person per month. Article 3 (Bonus): Each pawnshop should announce its annual business situation at the end of each year. If there is a surplus, after deducting official profits and expenses, 20% or 30% of the remaining profit will be allocated (20% if the agreed-upon profit is 8%). Article 4 (Commission): The commission charged by each pawnshop is stipulated as 2%. Any amount exceeding this should be retained. Article 5 (Allowance): The allowance for supplementing income from the old conditions should be abolished. However, allowances for special circumstances should still be retained. Article 6 (Vacancies): If any pawnshop dismisses an employee for cause, or an employee voluntarily resigns or dies, the vacancy must be filled by promoting an employee from within the pawnshop. Outsiders should not be hired to fill the vacancy unless absolutely necessary. Article 7 (Dismissal): Employees of any pawnshop should not be dismissed without major fault. If dismissed, they must be paid the usage due to them and appropriate travel expenses. Article 8 (Closure): If a pawnshop owner closes the business for any reason and dismisses employees, each employee must be paid a dismissal fee of 300 yuan, and the full usage should be calculated based on the existing inventory. However, if the losses are too great, the amount may be reduced. Before the pawnshop is dissolved, the management should pay double the salary. Article 9 (Working Hours): The daily working hours of each pawnshop employee should not exceed nine hours, except on New Year's Eve (the time should be determined according to the customs of each pawnshop's area). Article 10 (Leave): Each pawnshop employee should have two months of paid leave per year. In the event of a wedding or funeral, leave may be taken at any time. Article 11 (Pension): If an employee of any pawnshop dies due to illness, the management must provide a pension based on the years of service. For those who have served in the pawnshop for less than ten years, a one-time pension of 100 yuan will be given, with the position retained for three months. For those who have served for more than ten years, 120 yuan will be given, with the position retained for six months. For those who have served for more than fifteen years, 160 yuan will be given, with the position retained for eight months. For those who have served for more than twenty years, 240 yuan will be given, with the position retained for one year. Those who sacrifice their lives on duty will be given a preferential pension. The benefits they were entitled to before their death and during the retention period must still be calculated and paid. Article 12 (Insurance): If employees have clothes and items, the pawnshop owner should provide insurance. This does not apply to uninsured items in the pawnshop. Article 13 (Public Welfare Fund): Each pawnshop will subsidize the workers' union's public welfare fund by one yuan per month, to be jointly managed by five representatives from labor and management. Article 14 (Holidays): Each pawnshop should close on National Day and New Year's holidays stipulated by the government. Article 15 (Effective Date): These conditions will take effect from the date of signing by both parties (the old agreement should be canceled on the effective date). December 21, 1930. Representatives of Shop Owners: Fang Minfu (acting for Yu Langxi), Yu Shaoqing, Cheng Rufu, Wu Jiemei, Mu Jingshan, Shen Linzhi. Representatives of Shop Employees: Wang Ganchen, Cheng Xingzhu, Jin Futian, Cheng Zijun. Representative of the Municipal Public Training Committee: Tao Baichuan. Representative of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau: Guo Yongxi. Recorder: Shi Shaohua.

Workers' Petition

Marching in Formation: Apart from the survey team, special team, maintenance team, transportation team, and personnel in charge of documentation, publicity, and general affairs who continued to work as usual, the remaining 200+ workers at the union assembled at the union hall at 1 p.m., divided into four teams led by team leaders Qian Huanying, Weng Kangfu, etc., and marched to the Party Headquarters to petition. Each person wore the workers' union symbol for identification. The team leaders held white flags in their hands. They marched in an orderly fashion, two abreast, before and after each other, through the streets, maintaining strict formation.

Losses at Cuiyuan: As the petitioning workers marched in formation to Wansheng Bridge south of Old West Gate, they saw that Cuiyuan Pawnshop was open for business as usual. Believing this to be a sabotage of the strike, the workers swarmed forward and knocked down one of the signboards hanging in front of the shop, and urged it to close. Subsequently, the manager came out and admitted that they would close immediately and promised not to open again during the workers' strike. The workers then re-formed and continued to the Municipal Party Headquarters. Upon arriving at the Party Headquarters, they stood in a row and shouted slogans such as "Support Workers' Representatives" and "Request the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau to Uphold Justice and Alleviate Labor Oppression." Despite the freezing wind and light rain, the workers stood upright on the wet ground in front of the Party Headquarters until the mediation concluded late at night before returning. Written Petition: While the conditions were being discussed and amended inside, the workers remained outside as it was inconvenient for them to enter. Therefore, they submitted a written petition, which stated: "We petition regarding the following matter. Because of the movement for better conditions, the management has consistently ignored us, forcing us to declare a strike on the eighteenth to awaken the management. The details have been reported to your esteemed headquarters, and we are grateful that your esteemed headquarters has specifically convened labor and management for mediation today. It has been four days since we went on strike, and the spiritual and financial losses are immeasurable. Moreover, in this severe weather, the impact on the economy of ordinary people is significant. Upon hearing that your esteemed headquarters had convened a mediation, the members were overjoyed, believing that our plight could be resolved and our poverty alleviated. However, we are mindful that the management is cunning by nature, and we fear that today's meeting will be another false hope. Therefore, we have specially organized a petitioning group to implore your esteemed headquarters to strictly order the management to reach a satisfactory resolution today so that the strike can be brought to an end today. It is not only the labor and management sides that will benefit from this. We are unable to express the urgency of our prayers and sincerely present this to the Public Training Committee of the Municipal Party Headquarters of the Chinese Nationalist Party, from the entire membership of the Pawn Industry Workers' Union of Shanghai."

Labor News

Prosecution: On the afternoon of the nineteenth, the four workers who were arrested by the Harbin police for advising Hexiang Pawnshop in East Jiaxing Road to close were transferred to the court. Cheng Guangzu, Wang Junyan, and Shao Chunsheng were sentenced to three weeks of detention. They declared their dissatisfaction and filed an appeal. The workers' union hired lawyers Yang Zhihao and Zhuang Yingxun to draft the appeal. However, due to it being Sunday yesterday, it was decided to first bail out the three sentenced individuals today and then file an appeal. As the three are currently detained in the Harbin police station, it is feared that the cold weather will cause them to become ill.

Union Assistance: Yesterday, representatives from the Sanyou Industrial Society Labor Union, Xia Zhongzhao, the Gold and Silver Foil Industry Labor Union, Liu Panchou, Wu Buyan, the Umbrella Industry Labor Union, Sheng Qingtong, the Western-Style Furniture Industry Labor Union, the Jiaxing Pawn Industry General Labor Union, and the Express Mail Telegraph, among others, sent their condolences. Over one hundred labor unions throughout Shanghai held a meeting at the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union yesterday afternoon at 1 p.m. to discuss providing assistance to the pawn industry striking workers. They resolved to: (1) Convene a city-wide labor representative conference on Thursday to organize a support association; (2) Jointly petition the Municipal Party Headquarters to earnestly order the management to amend the conditions; (3) Discuss the issue of the existence and abolition of the workers' union. The Joint Federation of Various Industries also issued a declaration.

Workers at Zhabei Chinese Merchants Public Bus Company on Slowdown Yesterday 106

Workers Demand Year-End Bonus

Ineffective Negotiation Between Both Parties

Although Bus Operated Normally Yesterday

Passengers Didn't Have to Buy Ticket

The crowdedness on Zhabei Chinese Merchants Public Bus, which runs between North Station, Jiangwan, Zhenru, etc., was rarely seen yesterday. All buses on various routes were fully loaded with passengers, crowded and impenetrable. Those who saw it thought it was a prosperous business, surpassing the past. However, the company side was at a loss, with worry written all over their faces. The reason why there were so many passengers was actually the result of the workers' slowdown, not the so-called booming business. Even worse, although the buses operated normally, the company not only had no income but also had to compensate for gasoline, tires, repairs, and other expenses, causing significant losses to the company. This is truly a unique aspect of the slowdown.

Slowdown Situation: Zhabei Public Buses usually start operating at 6 a.m. to carry passengers. Yesterday morning, the workers all arrived at the factory to work as usual, just like any other day, and all 26 buses on routes 1, 2, and 3 were dispatched. However, at around 7 a.m., they suddenly started the slowdown in unison. The ticket seller at the Baoshan Road intersection first put the tickets into the collection box and stopped issuing tickets. The buses operating on various routes also allowed passengers to board without buying tickets. The ticket sellers stood by with their hands in their sleeves, mingling with the passengers. Therefore, on the surface, no one knew that the public bus workers had slowed down.

Buses Were Crowded: Yesterday it rained. Even if the public buses on various routes were not on slowdown, the number of passengers would certainly be more than usual. However, after the news spread that the workers were on slowdown and passengers did not have to buy tickets, the number of passengers on each bus suddenly increased. Even those who had no intention of taking the bus boarded with the crowd. Each bus was stipulated to carry only 32 people, but now the number of passengers was at least 40 or 50, and some even doubled. The company side, upon learning of this, was deeply afraid that excessive loading would inevitably cause an accident, so they notified the police station to pay attention along the way. The company's losses yesterday were approximately 1,000 yuan.

Workers' Demands: The reason for the workers' slowdown was the demand for a year-end bonus and uniforms. The details are as follows: The Zhabei Chinese Merchants Public Bus Company has a total of 26 buses, divided into three routes: (Route 1) 11 buses running from Baoshan Road intersection to Jiangwan; (Route 2) 4 buses running between Qiujiang Road, Sichuan Road, and Xinzha Bridge; (Route 3) 11 buses running from Baoshan Road intersection to Zhenru and beyond. The three routes have more than 100 drivers and ticket sellers working in early and late shifts. On October 24, the workers held a meeting and resolved to demand that the company issue a year-end double salary and winter uniforms. On October 25, the workers' union submitted the request to the company. The company's reply stated that it was still too early to discuss year-end bonuses and that there would be a solution in the future. As for the winter uniforms, if thick woolen fabric was required, the cost would be borne half by the company and half by the workers. As a result, there was no outcome. Later, requests continued until the 17th of this month, seven times in total, but ultimately there was no progress.

Negotiation Process: After the 17th of this month, the majority of the workers advocated for a slowdown. Huang Zhongwen, the director of the company's transportation department, reported the workers' plan to the company authorities and began negotiations. The company then appointed Ren Zuojun as its representative to negotiate with the workers. As a result, the workers originally demanded a year-end double salary, with a minimum of 25 days of double pay per month. The company side's highest limit was to issue 15 days of bonus pay and could not increase it further. Thus, the negotiations were suspended and the two sides broke down. At 10 p.m. the night before last, the workers gathered at the workers' union to hold a meeting and resolved that all drivers and ticket sellers would uniformly slow down as a final demand, and petitioned the relevant Sixth District Party Headquarters, the Municipal Party Headquarters Public Training Committee, the Social Affairs Bureau, and other agencies to request mediation.

Party Headquarters Investigation: After the bus workers' slowdown, at 8:30 a.m., representatives Liang Guoming and Liu Shouchun were dispatched to the Municipal Party Headquarters to petition and reported the details of the slowdown. At 4 p.m., the Municipal Party Headquarters sent Zhou Funong as its representative to investigate everything at the Chinese Merchants Bus Workers' Union. The result was that the matter was of great importance, and the Municipal Party Headquarters would, together with the Social Affairs Bureau, send representatives to the company to conduct mediation tomorrow morning (today). The workers side decided at a meeting yesterday afternoon to continue the slowdown today. If the company prevents the buses on all routes from leaving the factory in the morning, they will report to the Public Security Bureau, claiming that the management is obstructing traffic and demanding that the Public Security Bureau ensure the safety of the workers, etc.

Company's Attitude: According to the company's statement, there are currently over 160 employees, with the monthly salary of drivers ranging from 25 yuan to 49 yuan, ticket sellers from 20 yuan to 24 yuan, and ticket inspectors from 35 yuan to 39 yuan. An additional salary increase of three days is added each month, and a bonus is calculated every six months. Any worker who has not committed any misconduct in six months can receive a bonus ranging from 30 yuan to 40 yuan. On average, 90% of the workers can receive this bonus. As for the issue of only allowing the issuance of a 15-day year-end bonus this time, it is because the company's finances this year have been greatly affected by the Jin Hui exchange rate, leading to high material costs and making it difficult to make ends meet. Even issuing a 15-day year-end bonus is a strain. However, because the two sides were unable to reach an agreement, the workers used the slowdown as a form of resistance. However, the union did not submit a request to the higher authorities for mediation in advance. They suddenly slowed down and arbitrarily drove the buses without stopping, collecting fares, or even freely entering the factory. The company has no way to stop this and can only await the authorities' disposition.

Labor's Petition: Yesterday, the Public Bus Workers' Union submitted a petition to the Sixth District Party Headquarters, the Municipal Party Headquarters Public Training Committee, and the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting mediation. The petition stated: "In order to report on the management's refusal to give a year-end double salary and all unreasonable oppression, we request that you promptly send personnel to mediate and prevent a major dispute between labor and management. It is our understanding that a year-end double salary is a common practice in all shops and factories throughout the country, and it is also the compensation that employers should provide. How prosperous an enterprise is in a year depends mostly on the labor of the workers. Therefore, labor and management have such a major and close relationship. There should be appropriate compensation for a year's hard work, which can not only encourage workers but also have a significant impact on business. Therefore, employers must uphold the spirit of labor-management cooperation and should automatically issue a year-end double salary without waiting for the workers' request. This can encourage workers and promote business development. However, the company is cunning by nature and uses all means of oppression without any sincerity in seeking labor-management cooperation. We will now present one or two examples to your department: (1) Uniforms are supposed to be issued by the company for both winter and summer. The company has requested that the union follow up on this year's winter uniforms. The company used a very cheap and thin fabric to make the winter uniforms. The fabric sample was viewed by all the workers, who believed that the uniforms represent the company and the spirit of the workers. The fabric sample proposed by the company was not only insufficient to enhance appearance but also insufficient to keep warm. The entire workforce objected, and after negotiation by the union, it was stopped. The company was then asked to make thick woolen uniforms, but the company firmly refused. After repeated negotiations by the union, they agreed to make woolen fabric, but the cost of the uniforms would have to be shared by the workers and deducted from their salaries. All members of the union, as the weather is getting colder and colder, cannot bear the cold in their summer uniforms. If they wear their own clothes, it is not allowed by the regulations, which is very harmful to their health. They had to reluctantly agree. As of today, the winter uniforms have not yet been put on. In China and foreign countries, employers provide uniforms, but the Chinese Merchants Public Bus Company is opening a new precedent. This shows that the company is using every means possible against its workers. (2) Regarding the year-end double salary, in October of this year, union members sent letters to the union requesting that the union ask the company to issue two months' salary. The union members found that factories, companies, and transportation businesses in the Zhabei area of Shanghai had been offering as much as three months, two months, one month, and even borrowing an additional month. Therefore, the request for two months was carefully discussed at the fourth general meeting on October 24 of this year, and it was decided that the time was not right to examine the situation of the company in the spirit of pure labor-management cooperation. After deliberation, it was decided to reduce the request to one month and sent representatives to the company to request it on October 25 of this year. The company replied that it was still too early and that the company was also considering the period, and that there was no fixed rule for issuing one month or even two months. The union representatives told all members that the company's reply would be able to meet the hopes of all workers, and all members were satisfied with this reply. Unexpectedly, the company intended to prevaricate. It has now been five or six times that they have requested the company, and the company first responded that it should be on the 12th, then the 17th, and finally the 15th. This erratic change is too different from the requirements of all employees, and the company's talks are not sufficient to gain the trust of the workers. Therefore, all employees are extremely angry and are eager to take the most serious measures against the company. The union, considering the company's business relationship, made every effort to facilitate transportation and should be responsible for negotiating with the company again to achieve the goal of all workers. However, the workers are approaching the end of the year and cannot wait. They have been questioning the union every day. Therefore, the union sent representatives to the company again yesterday for a final negotiation, but the company firmly insisted on 15 days, which is still far from the requirements of all workers, and as a result, there was no outcome. Therefore, the workers became even more angry upon hearing this, and decided to take countermeasures. As the union believes that the matter is of great importance and cannot bear this heavy responsibility, in addition to trying to persuade and stop them within the past two days, we are hereby presenting this petition to request your department to promptly send personnel to mediate in order to avoid a major dispute and ensure the people's expectations are met. We are extremely grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Sixth District Party Headquarters, the Municipal Party Headquarters Public Training Committee, and the Social Affairs Bureau of the Chinese Nationalist Party. Shanghai Chinese Merchants Public Bus Workers' Union."

Liquor Store Labor Strike Escalates 107

Declared Strike Yesterday

The liquor store employees in this city have been under pressure from the Second District Baijiu Tax Collection Office, which has nearly led to a slowdown. Yesterday, because the Tax Collection Office had not yet responded, they officially declared a strike. Details are recorded below:

Negotiation Process: Yesterday, following the resolution, the trade association dispatched representatives Huang Yuming, Zhang Guanshou, and Shi Youqing to negotiate with the Tax Collection Office. However, the director of the office, Li Guangzhen, knowing he was in the wrong, avoided meeting them. The assistant director, Zhu Houfu, received them, but Mr. Zhu stated that he had no authority to respond and could not negotiate. The three representatives had no choice but to withdraw without any results.

Declaration of Strike: After the management representatives reported the situation, the workers at the union were indignant. They believed that only a strike would warn the Tax Collection Office. Therefore, they immediately issued an order declaring a strike. The membership meeting was held at 2 p.m. yesterday, the fifth general membership meeting. Hu Guzhen was elected chairman, and the formalities were performed. First, the chairman reported that the negotiations with the Tax Collection Office had been insincere in accepting their demands, so he immediately declared a strike. Then, they began to discuss: (1) After the strike, all employees must strictly abide by order and not go out under false pretenses. (2) If this strike is not resolved satisfactorily, we will not resume work. (3) The Tax Collection Office should compensate for the losses caused by the strike. The meeting was adjourned after the discussion.

Baoshan County Prepares for New Year's Day Celebration Conference 112

Baoshan County government agencies held a meeting at the county government at 1 p.m. yesterday to discuss the preparations for celebrating the National Calendar's 20th New Year's Day. Attendees included Qiu Mingjiu, Ji Zhonghe, Zhang Jingshi, Wang Tongchuan, Bei Jietai, Yin Xiangsun, Ge Zuwang, Wang Qingtao, etc. County Magistrate Qiu presided over the meeting, and Zhang Ruyu recorded the minutes. The resolutions are recorded below: (1) How to propose and promote the National Calendar New Year. Resolutions: (1) All New Year's greetings, ancestral worship, Spring Festival banquets, etc., held by the people at the end and beginning of the old lunar year should be moved to around the National Calendar New Year. (2) The County Party Headquarters' Propaganda Department should directly distribute Spring Festival couplets. (3) Spring Festival couplets and national party flags should be posted and hung at the entrances of all agencies, organizations, district offices, township offices, etc. (4) The district offices, township heads, etc., should each purchase a new calendar book and have the county government purchase and distribute them, with the funds deducted from the district heads. (5) Earnestly guide the stores in each township and town to follow the central government's regulations to close their accounts at the end of the National Calendar year. (6) During the National Calendar New Year, each district, town, and township should do their best to promote proper entertainment. (7) All agencies, organizations, stores, etc., should be closed for three days from February 1st to 3rd on the National Calendar. (2) How to ban the lunar New Year. Resolutions: (1) Strictly prohibit the sale of old calendars. (2) All agencies, organizations, stores, etc., should work as usual at the end and beginning of the lunar year. (3) During the end and beginning of the lunar year, the setting off of firecrackers should be strictly prohibited, except for special celebrations. (4) During the end and beginning of the lunar year, monks and Taoists should be prohibited from collecting money and giving away superstitious lunar items. (5) Beggars and vagrants are prohibited from forcibly asking for money under false pretenses at the end and beginning of the lunar year.

November Foreign Exchange Rates, Year 19 114

Unstable Foreign Exchange Market

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau announced the foreign exchange rates for the month. Initially, due to the ongoing autumn racing season in the city, many adopted a wait-and-see attitude, resulting in sluggish trading and a stagnant market. Subsequently, both overt and covert tightening occurred, with repeated reports of declines in Bombay silver prices. Furthermore, due to substantial settlements by the Ministry of Railways and British-American Tobacco Company, the downward trend was severe. The highest listed exchange rate for British currency was 1 shilling, 7 pence, and 25, the lowest was 1 shilling, 6 pence, and 625. The highest exchange rate for US currency was 39 yuan, the lowest was 37 yuan, 6 jiao, 2 fen, and 5 li. The highest exchange rate for Japanese currency was 1 liang, 3 qian, 1 fen, and 7.5 li, the lowest was 1 liang, 2 qian, and 7.5 fen. The highest exchange rate for French currency was 993 francs, the lowest was 965 francs. All exchange rates were higher than the previous month, with British currency increasing by 0.038, US currency by 0.06, Japanese currency by 0.019, and French currency by 0.017. The overall index rose by 0.018.

Establishment of Jardine Matheson Stevedores Club 115

Jardine Matheson & Co., Ltd., a British firm, operates 41 Jianghai shipping vessels in China. The company's stevedoring department has numerous employees. To unite their strength and improve their work and lives, they initiated the organization of a Stevedores Club, which has been unanimously approved. Zeng Shanren has been publicly elected as the appointee, and Ye Bingkui and Zhong Delin as standing committee members. The club's address has been set at No. 6, Peiguo Lane, Dasheng Lane, Minguo Road. The matter has been submitted to the Seamen's Union for record-keeping. It has been decided that the New Year's Day will be the day of the club's establishment. All comrades on the ships have been notified to attend the founding ceremony at that time, and the Municipal Party Department and the Seamen's Union have been invited to send personnel to provide guidance.

Song Zi-Liang Discusses Dredging 116

Mr. Song Zi-Liang, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Director of the Dredging Bureau, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning. A reporter from the Guomin News Agency happened to meet him at a friend's house. Mr. Song said that the dredging of the Suzhou Creek will be implemented soon. He has consulted with business leaders regarding the dredging of the Wusong River mouth and it has been decided that about two large dredging vessels will be required, each costing 2 million yuan. These funds are planned to be obtained from foreign vessels entering the port by appropriately increasing the dredging fee for foreign vessels. If this plan is successful, the largest merchant ships will be able to enter and exit the Wusong port, which will greatly contribute to the prosperity of Shanghai. He believes that in another ten or twenty years, Shanghai can reach the third position among the world's largest commercial ports. Finally, Mr. Song also told the reporter that he regretted not being able to serve his elderly and ailing mother often, so he strongly requested to resign from the position of Director of General Affairs. It is said that Minister Wang deeply relies on Mr. Song's orderly handling of the department's affairs and is therefore trying hard to retain him.

China Wireless Engineering School 117

The China Wireless Engineering School was founded by Shanghai gentry and merchants such as Yu Qiaqing. The teaching is serious, the facilities are complete, and the school has been operating for two years with remarkable achievements. Graduates of the engineering and telecommunications departments have been introduced by the school to obtain considerable employment, with some serving as radio officers on major ships and others serving as engineers in various companies and radio stations. The Wireless Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications recently recruited radio officers and machine operators. Many students from the school applied for the positions and were accepted, which is a testament to the school's excellent performance. It is heard that the school's spring enrollment examination will be held on December 28 and January 11 next year. The school address is No. 855, Ximengnala Road, Aiduya Road.

Petition to Ban Illegal Commercial Organizations 119

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a document to the Municipal Party Department, the Civil Training Committee, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, stating: Regarding the matter of petitioning, Article 11 of the Municipal Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Organizational Procedures promulgated in Civil Training Committee Notice No. 7 states that according to the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Reorganization Procedures of the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee, after the restructured trade association receives the certificate from the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee, it should immediately submit the certificate along with the association's constitution, membership roster, staff resumes, and other survey forms to this committee for certification in accordance with the above procedures. Article 12 states that after the trade association receives the approval decree with the above certification, it should immediately apply for registration with the Social Affairs Bureau. Previously, the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee had reorganized the commercial organizations in this city in accordance with the National Government's decision on industrial and commercial trade associations, and those whose organizations were not fully compliant with current laws and regulations were ordered to restructure in accordance with the law, and those with several organizations in the same industry in one area were ordered to merge in accordance with the law. Only after the reorganization was completed were certificates issued separately. After the establishment of the Chamber of Commerce, the Chamber has continued to handle the organizations that were not yet ready for reorganization by the previous Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee according to the previous plan. Therefore, commercial organizations established before the reorganization that have not received a certificate from the Chamber or the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee must have the following situations: although they have registered with the previous Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee, their organization fundamentally conflicts with current laws and regulations, and there is no possibility of ordering them to restructure or merge; the organization itself has never agreed to accept the letter ordering reorganization or merger; those that meet the second situation have violated the regulations of the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law that require restructuring within a time limit and only allow one association to be established in one area, and therefore cannot be recognized as a legitimate organization and should be banned. Furthermore, according to the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Organizational Procedures promulgated by the Civil Training Committee, if it is a newly established organization, it must go through two procedures of permission and registration; if it is a restructured organization, it must go through two procedures of certification and registration. If the commercial organizations have not gone through the procedures of permission and establishment or registration with the competent authorities, their reorganization has not been completed, and according to Article 4 of the People's Organizations Establishment Procedures and Article 5 of the Municipal Industrial and Commercial Organizations Registration Rules, they should be revoked and banned. Therefore, according to the above-mentioned situations, all those (1) who have not been issued a permit certificate by the Civil Training Committee, (2) who have not registered with the Social Affairs Bureau, (3) who have not been ordered to restructure or merge by the previous Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee or the Chamber, or who have failed to accept the order to restructure or merge, should be banned. However, it is currently found that commercial organizations of this type in this city still handle affairs in the name of their organizations as usual, which is not enough to respect the law. In addition to the organizations of various industries with more than one industry or more than one district that have been registered with the previous Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee, the Chamber should immediately issue a letter ordering them to handle matters in accordance with the articles added to the Industrial and Commercial Trade Union that were passed by the Legislative Yuan on August 2 of this year. It is appropriate to submit a written proposal for the categories of organizations of various industries that have not been completed and should be banned for your review and approval. Please thoroughly investigate and announce the ban one by one, ordering them to end and disband immediately. If they still disobey and secretly collect membership fees, they will be prosecuted for fraud. At the same time, the legally organized organizations of various industries will be published in the newspaper to emphasize the law and avoid confusion. Whether this is appropriate, please instruct us to follow. This is truly in the public interest.

Foreign Ships Greatly Reduce Lake Silk Freight 120

Due to Lower Silk Exports Than Last Year

Reduced by Six or Seven Taels of Silver Per Piece

Lake silk exports are the largest part of China's foreign trade. This year, due to repeated disturbances in various silk factories, the number of exports has sharply decreased, and the high price of gold and the low price of silver have affected foreign ships. It is found that the number of Lake silk transported to Europe in the past month has decreased by 6,000 pieces compared to the same period last year. The export business of the British and French mail ship companies in this city has always been dominated by Chinese silk exports. In recent months, the amount of silk carried has been decreasing day by day. The shipping companies have discussed this matter many times. Although it is related to market conditions, the high cost of freight also has an impact. Therefore, it is proposed to reduce the price of silk transported to Europe to an unprecedented level. The freight rate for Lake silk has never fluctuated by more than two or three qian at most, but this time it has dropped by six or seven taels of silver per piece, which is rare in recent years. Yesterday, the British and French shipping companies agreed to allow the new price to be reduced from New Year's Day. The new price has been set and has been issued to the silk merchants to settle this matter and encourage the transportation of silk to Europe. The new and old prices are recorded below:

Red Cross Receives Disaster Report from Xianyang Yesterday 121

The Chinese Red Cross Society received a telegram from Chen Bolong and other citizens of Xianyang, Shaanxi, yesterday, reporting the tragic disaster situation, which is hereby disclosed: "Our Qin has suffered from chaos for a long time. The calamities of war and famine have lasted for two years. The number of people who have died cannot be counted. In terms of natural disasters, all counties are the same. In terms of man-made disasters, Xianyang is unique. Because it is located on a thoroughfare, the supply and requisition are extremely heavy, and the people's bones are scraped and their marrow sucked to meet the support, leading to bankruptcy and no means of making a living. What is even more unbearable is that when the soldiers arrive, they will count the number of mouths and search for all the vehicles and horses needed. Therefore, agriculture is delayed, and there are few granaries in the households. Water and drought occur from time to time. Other counties have years of partial flooding, but the corvée is particularly heavy. Xianyang rarely has years without flooding. The vitality has long been lost, and the suffering is particularly severe. Even in years of good harvest, there are many hungry people, let alone years of continuous crop failure, with barren land for thousands of miles. The wood of the tall buildings is completely destroyed for firewood, and the fields that stretch for miles have no owners to sell them to. Fathers abandon their sons, and husbands abandon their wives. It is difficult to keep the flesh and blood whole. They say goodbye with tears. Corpses are piled up, and the souls of the neighbors are miserable. In addition, the Feng army requisitioning is as fierce as wolves and tigers, targeting the households with the last bit of resources. The soldiers still impose taxes on the people who sleep in the wind and dew, and they cannot avoid donating wheels. Therefore, disaster-stricken households are everywhere, and refugees are wailing. It is a heart-wrenching sight. Unexpectedly, during the central government's chaos, there are treacherous and evil people such as Zhen Shoushan and Yao Zhenqian who took the opportunity to steal and manipulate, driving the masses to pretend to be the will of the people and assisting the rebels, betraying and reversing constantly, disregarding the catastrophe of the hometown, and even allowing the bandits to ravage, burn, kill, and rob with inhumanity. They imitate the old tricks of the warlords and create feudal dreams with blatant arrogance, actually resisting orders, and even leading to the emptiness of the loom and swallowing of bran and chaff. They want to break the firewood and firewood, but the room has long been transformed into a grave. They are about to exchange sons and divide their daughters, but the young ones have already become hungry ghosts. In villages of ten households, the smoke and fire are cut off. In areas of hundreds of miles, dogs cannot be heard. The days ahead are long. The dead cannot be brought back to life, and what will the living do to survive? Now that the national army has entered the customs, the demonic atmosphere has been swept away, and the chief culprits have been beheaded. I hope that more people will be freed from their upside-down situation. However, those who are to be pacified are helpless and waiting to die, and the number of refugees without a home is increasing. Small bandits are still lurking in remote areas, and the harvest is poor. I implore you to show compassion and provide relief to those in distress, cut off the source of evil, and restore the vitality of the people. Please also instruct the military officers to send strong troops to earnestly pacify and eliminate the root causes, so that future generations can share peace and enjoy the benefits. This telegram is filled with sorrow and gratitude. We sincerely wish you well." Signed by Chen Bolong, Zhao Ru, Ruizheng, Wang Youhan, Wang Jitao, Wang Renfu, Yang Shoubo, Cheng Liancheng, Zhao Dianqing, Cheng Zhilian, Gao Jiuru, Chuan Linguish, Chen Qingyu, Cheng Shisheng, Bian Yuezhi, Zhu Shaoshan, Ji Kunshan, Liu Ruiting, and others from Xianyang County.

Appeal for Relief from Banditry in Suqian 122

The Jiangsu Provisional Relief Association received a plea for relief from the Suqian Provisional Disaster Relief Association, which roughly stated: "Since the restoration, Suqian has suffered from water, drought, and banditry every year, but this year's water and banditry disasters are the most severe. It is flooded from the north by the confluence of the Yi and Si Rivers, and from the east by the overflow of the Shu River. In addition, there has been continuous rain for a month, turning hundreds of miles of north-south into a swamp. Eight or nine out of ten people cannot make a living. Moreover, bandits have risen up everywhere. The west of Suining, the south bordering Wansui, and the east to Siyang are all occupied by bandits, who break into villages and attack fortresses, killing and burning at will, and countless people have died. The old and young who have been kidnapped have either died of hunger or been tortured to death with knives. Corpses are piled up, which is a tragic sight. Fortunately, the 52nd Division arrived in Suqian and severely suppressed the bandits. When the bandits retreated, the burning and killing were even more terrible. Dozens of households were burned, and thirty or forty people were killed or injured. There are ruins everywhere, and not even dogs or chickens remain. Those who are fortunate enough to escape are lying weak and helpless in the wilderness, waiting to die. Those who have fled elsewhere have no home to return to. Moreover, wheat has not yet been sown, and there will be no hope for next year. Alas, my people of Suqian have suffered this natural disaster and have also suffered from banditry. In this severe winter, without clothes or food, how can they survive the year? We implore you to quickly bestow kindness and compassion to save the people from disaster. We are at the end of our road and we plead a hundred times over."

Post Office Does Not Mail Crepe Packages 124

Due to Ministry Order Prohibiting

The General Post Office stated that crepe packages have previously self-ignited in transit, causing significant losses. Although the dyes have been improved, experts have tested them and it is still difficult to guarantee that there is no danger. Therefore, it recently petitioned the Ministry of Communications to ask whether it could refuse to accept and mail them. It is heard that the office received a Ministry order yesterday stating that the prohibition on accepting and mailing will continue to be implemented in order to emphasize postal transportation and ensure safety.

(5) The union's finances are running a deficit. It was resolved to submit the matter to the members' meeting for resolution.

(6) The accountant will prepare the union's financial statement. It was resolved to submit it to the supervisory committee for review.

(7) The ticket sales department's exchange of copper coins for silver dollars at settlement does not follow market prices. It was resolved that the union should negotiate with the company to ensure that calculations are based on market prices.

(1) The Pawnshop Workers' Union requested the union to send representatives to their association during the strike. It was resolved to appoint Yu Ting and Zhang Gui as representatives.

(5) The executive committees of various warehouse branches requested negotiations with the bureau regarding unpaid wages. It was resolved that the executive directors would go to the bureau on Monday, the 22nd, to urge payment.

(6) The organization division reported that membership registration had been completed for all warehouses except Xinzhan, which had not yet submitted the registration form. It was resolved that the Xinzhan Branch Executive Committee should expedite the submission.

(7) The Mutual Aid Committee reported on the investigation of the unemployment benefits for Hua Warehouse member Chen Shaosu. It was resolved to instruct the general affairs division to issue 30 yuan in unemployment benefits according to the old regulations.

Ad Hoc Motions:

(1) The executive committee proposed preparing for the New Year's celebration. It was resolved to be handled by the general affairs division, the publicity division, and the entertainment committee.

Yesterday, the Cotton Weaving Workers' Union held a representative meeting, attended by more than thirty representatives. Comrade Zhong Quan, a representative of the Municipal Party Committee, attended to provide guidance. Kun Qiu was elected as chairman.

Shanghai Had Snow Pellets Yesterday 134

The Weather Turned Suddenly Cold

The city has been experiencing continuous overcast and rainy weather, and the climate has gradually turned cold. Yesterday, the day before the winter solstice, the sky was suddenly covered with dark clouds, a northerly wind howled, and fine rain drizzled. Around 1:35 PM, snow pellets suddenly fell for about ten minutes and then stopped. This was the first time seeing snow this winter. As a result, the weather felt particularly harsh, and the Fahrenheit temperature dropped sharply to 41 degrees, six degrees lower than the previous day.

Chen Shifan Escapes Danger 135

Chen Sends a Letter to the Newspaper

Escaped Danger Yesterday from Kidnappers

Chen Shifan, the Ningbo native and owner of the Chenlinji Construction Company, residing at 114 Rue de la P. Stone in the French Concession, was kidnapped by bandits around 9 PM the night before last (the 19th) at the entrance of the Fuzhili alley on Pingwang Street in the Public Concession. Details were reported in this newspaper. Unexpectedly, at around 1 AM yesterday morning, Chen, taking advantage of the kidnappers' deep sleep, single-handedly escaped from the bandits' den on Rue Ratard, climbing over the wall with a ladder. He then took a rickshaw directly home and reported the situation to the French Concession Police Station. The detectives dispatched by the captain went to the den to arrest the bandits, but they had already fled after hearing the news. Upon investigation, the bandits' den was located at the intersection of Rue Ratard and Avenue Joffre. The house was very small and the location extremely quiet. It was an unrented shop fronting the street, with the street number being 330. The storefront was tightly locked, and the bandits used it as a temporary ransom holding facility. They used a bamboo ladder to enter and exit through the rear wall. The detectives found the house empty and reported back to the captain. Some detectives were then dispatched to stand guard. Yesterday afternoon, just as this newspaper's reporter was about to investigate the scene, they received a letter from the kidnap victim Chen Shifan, detailing the kidnapping and escape. The original letter is transcribed below:

"Respectfully, after being kidnapped the night before last, I was held in a small house at the intersection of Rue Ratard and Avenue Joffre. This house is an unrented shop fronting the street, tightly locked, and used by the bandits as a den. The bandits used a bamboo ladder to enter and exit through the rear wall. Once inside, I was guarded by two bandits in the kitchen under the house. They sat on the floor. By last night, I had been awake for a whole day and night, and I was exhausted. I then tempted them to fall asleep and planned a desperate gamble. The bandits agreed, and shortly after, the two bandits fell into a deep sleep. I thought this opportunity was rare and easy, so I slowly moved and found a bamboo ladder, climbed over the wall, and escaped. After running a few steps, I saw a rickshaw and hastily took it home. I immediately informed the French Concession Police Station, and they dispatched detectives to arrest the bandits, but they had already learned of it and fled. I am merely making a living in the construction industry and have a very small scale, so I have never contracted large projects. The house I live in is also rented land, built by myself. This newspaper reported that I also operate real estate and construction businesses, which is quite impressive, but this is not true. The Rongyangli Commercial Real Estate Company is a small general association organized by me and others, entirely for entertainment purposes and has no other functions. Therefore, I am writing this letter to clarify the true situation. Chen Shifan, respectfully. Twenty-first day of the twelfth month of the nineteenth year [of the Republic]."

It was noted that two kidnapping cases occurred on the 19th. One was the case of Ding Ziren, the owner of the Fuxin Flour Factory No. 2 on West Suzhou Road. Ding is currently still being held captive, and there is no news from the bandits' den. Now Chen has unexpectedly escaped, which is fortunate. Some are fortunate, some are not.

Zhu Haixiang, a native of Fenghua, 34 years old, residing at Song Debao's house in the first alley of Baoxing Road in Zhabei, was walking along Jing'an Temple Road near the Racecourse at around 6 PM last night when he was suddenly struck by a car with the Concession registration number 9806 driven by a British soldier, knocking him to the ground. Soft Entry, Hard Exit Robbery 139

Sneaking into the House and Looting

This is Called the Soft Entry, Hard Exit Method

The Circumstances of the Two Pawnshops Being Robbed are Similar

After Investigation, the Three Thieves are Transferred for Interrogation

The Gongchang Pawnshop at 1072 Pingliang Road was robbed at 2:30 AM on the 13th of last month by robbers who entered through the roof. Each held a handgun and looted the gold jewelry. The shop employees woke up from their dreams, but dared not speak out because the thieves were armed. After looting, the thieves took long gowns, dressed themselves, opened the back door, and fled. After the owner inspected the damage, the losses were no less than five thousand yuan. He reported the case to the police station to investigate. The conduct of this type of thief is different from other thieves, who often rob at night but do not enter through the door. Among them, it is called soft entry, hard exit. During the summer, the Wanji Pawnshop at 1913 Avenue Edouard VII was also robbed by soft entry, hard exit thieves, losing five bolts of silk, a loss of only about two hundred gold, not as large as Gongchang. Both cases have not yet been solved. Recently, the French Concession police captured three thieves and transferred them to the French Concession Court for sentencing. Xu Ali and Duan Atian were each sentenced to five years of imprisonment, and Gong Amao was expelled from the Concession. The three thieves were the masterminds behind the robberies of the Gongchang and Wanji shops. The Yangshupu Police Station transferred them from the French Concession Police Station the day before yesterday and brought out two bolts of silk, the original stolen goods, from a pawnshop. They were then transferred to the Special District Court. The owners sent employees to the court to describe the robbery and identify Xu Ali. Judge Ge asked Xu, and the thief admitted that he was invited by the fugitives Dai Aer and Mao Haixiang to rob Gongchang. After the robbery, he received 175 yuan. Mao gave him another 100 yuan to give to Duan Atian, because Duan had participated in the plan beforehand. As for the Wanji case, he did it with the fugitive Chen Donglin, and he received two bolts of silk, which are the ones that have been brought out today. Duan Atian testified that before robbing Gongchang, he discussed it at the Xinhua Hotel on Avenue Edward VII. Xu came to invite him temporarily, but he refused to go. Two days later, Mao Hailin gave him 100 yuan. The court ordered the defendants to be detained for further investigation.

Another Accusation of Fraud Against Fuhua Bank 140

The Fuhua Bank at 8 Jiujiang Road was falsely established by swindler Liu Jiugao, Liu Ying, along with Westerner Yaguluo De, Huang Zhitang, and Cao Liugen, and others, who used newspaper advertisements to solicit employees to defraud guarantee money. The victim Huang Bingyan reported the case, and the Special District Court repeatedly summoned the Chinese defendants, Liu and others, to court for trial, and ordered them to post bail. However, Huang was not the only victim. After Huang filed the lawsuit, Xu Shousu from Ningbo, and Yuan Shilin and Gu Jinsheng from the local area, also suffered the same losses as Huang. Therefore, they followed Huang's example and hired lawyers to sue the Special Court. According to Xu's testimony in the trial the day before yesterday, he saw an advertisement on July 28th recruiting employees, and since he was unemployed, he went to visit and contacted the bank manager, Liu Jiugao. They agreed to pay a guarantee of 1,000 taels and signed a contract. He started working on August 13th. After being there for a month, he found nothing to do and felt suspicious. He resigned voluntarily, but Jiugao repeatedly evaded the issue of canceling the contract and returning the guarantee. On October 30th, he suddenly wanted to use the guarantee as a loan, and he realized that he had been defrauded. Yuan Shilin claimed that he saw an advertisement for two accountants and contacted Jiugao at Fuhua. He demanded a guarantee of 1,000 yuan, saying that it was okay to use real estate deeds instead of cash, and boasted that the capital was 500,000, so there would be no fraud. So he first paid 500 yuan, and the remaining money was handed over to Liu Ying. Gu Jinsheng claimed that he joined as a trainee and handed over a guarantee of 200 yuan to Jiugao. Cao Liugen was the director of the cash section of Fuhua. Only the defendant Liu Jiugao appeared in court, claiming that Liu Ying was his son-in-law, and the position of manager was held by Liu Ying. He was a doctor and denied any knowledge of the fraud. Judge Wu Tingqi ordered the defendant to post bail and try the case together with the one filed by Huang Bingrong.

1. False accusations of divorce, mediation hopeless, requesting a speedy legal ruling. This case stems from the plaintiff Dong Yu's lawsuit against the defendant Jiang Youzhi, alleging that she has long suffered from lung disease and requesting a divorce. The court has held two trials and ordered mediation, showing the fairness and impartiality of the court. The plaintiff's uncle, Dong Kang, invited the plaintiff to his house for negotiations several times. The defendant also expressed her opinions to Dong Kang: (1) If she is to be welcomed back for cohabitation, the previous treatment must be improved, and she must not continue to live in the pavilion, be treated with jealousy, and be treated worse than a maidservant; (2) If they live separately, the necessary living expenses for the mother and daughter and the daughter's marriage expenses when she grows up must be effectively guaranteed and must not be搪塞 with empty words leading to no way to collect; (3) If the above two items can be fulfilled, the plaintiff should write another letter allowing her to unite with others, abandoning his rights and not interfering. The plaintiff replied that he would welcome her back after the court's ruling, making a humorous statement and leaving. In such a case, who should bear the responsibility for the insincere mediation? Seeing the Min Guo Daily on the 17th, the plaintiff submitted a strange account of the original situation in the plea to request summons, and those who are difficult to silence is divided into three points, carefully debated as follows: (1) Knowing in advance that the marriage with Ms. Lu was out of obedience to the elders, and accepting this marriage, it was discovered that the former Judicial Chief Dong Kang was the plaintiff's uncle, and he relied on his cultivation to have today. In the 10th year of the Republic, the plaintiff served as an assigned secretary in the Shandong Higher Court. He knew that the Liu family in Changzhou had a daughter to be married, so he asked the Liu's adopted daughter, Ms. Chi, to be a matchmaker. Ms. Li did not agree, but the defendant's aunt was the eldest daughter-in-law of the Liu family, so she pulled the defendant to be a matchmaker. Immediately, she sent a photo for review and obtained her consent. In the autumn, the engagement was made in Dong Kang's Beijing residence. At that time, one matchmaker was her brother-in-law, Mr. Bao, and the other was Fan Zhaochang. That winter, she heard that the plaintiff had married the adopted daughter of the Lu family in Haimen in Jinan. Her aunt sent a letter to rebuke Dong Kang, who immediately summoned the plaintiff to Beijing and tried to persuade him to dissolve the marriage with the Jiang family to avoid future entanglements. The plaintiff insisted that there was no problem with Ms. Jiang as his wife and Ms. Lu as his concubine, and ordered him to write a letter. After the plaintiff returned, he entrusted his cousin Dong Banggan, who was a prosecutor, to send a letter to Ms. Chi proving the status of嫡庶. The original letter was sent to the south and preserved by the defendant's mother's family. This is the real situation when the engagement was made. The national marriage system has long been changed from the old law, and even parents can hardly interfere extremely. How can a family member force a marriage based on the status of a family member? Such a change of facts is like a dream. (2) The lawyer Lu's letter is referred to as a severance of all ties. After returning to her husband's home, she was not treated equally due to Ms. Lu's obstruction. At that time, relatives and friends urged the defendant to file a lawsuit for bigamy. The defendant was born into a famous family and was well-versed in her mother's teachings, remembering the meaning of one marriage and relying on it for life. She could not bear to do this. After that, she was abandoned outside many times, which cannot be described in writing. Finally, she lived in the Liu family in Changzhou for more than a year, and Dong Kang mediated. She only received 30 yuan before and after, while Ms. Lu lived in Shanghai.

The daily necessities and clothing were so different that they seemed to be in different worlds. How can there be any kindness or righteousness on the plaintiff's side? Finally, she had to entrust lawyer Lu Hongyi of Suzhou to send a letter questioning the matter. The support of husband and wife is recorded in the Civil Code. This is also the right given to the defendant by law to assert her rights. Does this constitute a condition for divorce? (3) 3,000 taels should be compensated for the marriage loss. The marriage was in the autumn of the eleventh year of the Republic, and everything was done hastily. She was married into the defendant's home. The engagement gifts and jewelry were four pieces. Three days later, she claimed that they were borrowed from relatives and returned them. In addition, there were no newly made clothes. The cost of the day was roughly estimated to be no more than 300 yuan. A few days later, she went north with him. All the travel expenses were borrowed by the defendant, 40 yuan was used and has not been returned. Today, men and women are being encouraged to be equal. She has been subjected to such oppression and abuse by a young man from the north. Finally, she wants to compensate her with 3,000 taels. Is it because men should have a superior position? The most ridiculous thing is that the Dong Yu statement was published in the newspaper on the same day. There are words in the text of forging documents and wantonly attacking the deceased wife. Asia Hotel Owner Wang Tingxiang Accused of Bigamy by Wife 146

Marries Concubine Due to Wife's Infertility

Concubine Does Not Dare to Presume

Judge Still Hopes for Reconciliation

The Asia Hotel on Guangdong Road is owned by Wang Tingxiang from Ningbo. Wang had already married Yang Zhishan's daughter, Xiuzhen. However, feeling incomplete, last March he married Lou Ruizhen, a prostitute from Hangzhou. Now, Xiuzhen has accused him of bigamy at the Special District Local Court. The day before yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi convened a hearing. According to Yang Xiuzhen's complaint, the defendant married Lou Ruizhen on March 18th. She, being bedridden at the time, heard the news and, despite her illness, rushed to the Asia Hotel. She saw the hall brilliantly lit with candles and a grand banquet with over a hundred guests joyously drinking. Below the stage, various performances were staged to entertain the guests. After a while, Lou Ruizhen, dressed in festive attire, went to the guests to offer wine. Although she, the plaintiff, did not witness the wedding with her own eyes, many relatives and friends did. However, they all sided with the defendant and were unwilling to uphold justice. When the defendant sent out invitations, people had tried to dissuade him, but he not only refused to listen but also beat and humiliated her, even tearing out several strands of her hair, which she is still hiding. As she spoke, she opened her package to show the strands of black hair. She continued, saying that since marrying Lou, the defendant had abandoned her and neglected her. Because she lacked living expenses, she had to ask the Asia Hotel's accountant for funds. Regardless of how small the amount was, if the defendant found out, he would not only abuse her but also suspend the accountant. Such instances were too numerous to list. He openly abandoned his wife to remarry, and even abused his legal wife. She requested that he be punished according to the law to uphold justice and maintain social order. When questioned, Wang Tingxiang confessed that because the plaintiff had never given birth, he took Lou as a concubine. There was no wedding ceremony held, nor did he send out invitations or hold a banquet. The plaintiff's claims were not entirely true. Lou Ruizhen testified that she was 25 years old and had been a prostitute in Huile Lane for 17 years. She met Wang Tingxiang in February of that year and then became his concubine. Initially, Wang rented a place for her, and she met with the plaintiff several times. They were harmonious with each other. The plaintiff herself knew she could not bear children and hoped she would give birth to an heir as soon as possible to avoid becoming an ancestor without descendants. They traveled to West Lake together and took a photo (the photo was submitted as evidence). From this, it can be seen that their relationship was extremely harmonious. She, coming from a brothel, was content to be a concubine. She would not dare to presume or become an enemy of the person who rescued her. There was indeed no wedding ceremony held. However, on that day, she moved from another place to the Asia Hotel, and Tingxiang's friends sent gifts for the move, so he also prepared wine to thank them. The defendant invited his friends Shen Ziliang, Zhang Zipei, Hu Mingchun, and others to testify that the wine that evening was indeed prepared by Wang to express his gratitude to those who gave gifts for the relocation. Because both parties held differing opinions, Judge Wu ordered them to reconcile privately. If reconciliation failed, another hearing would be scheduled.

Silver Dollar Exchange Rate Increases 148

The exchange rate for silver dollars in the local northern and southern markets decreased several times last week, with each silver dollar exchanging for 260 copper coins and each small silver dollar (i.e., five double dimes) exchanging for ten cents, plus 23 or 24 copper coins. Starting yesterday, the rate suddenly increased. The exchange rates posted by various money shops and cigarette paper shops showed each silver dollar exchanging for 270 or 268-9 copper coins, each small silver dollar exchanging for five double dimes plus 260 or 70 copper coins, and each double dime exchanging for 48 or 49 copper coins, an increase of 70-80 coins compared to the previous day's rate.

They also privately sold opium. The first precinct of the fourth district of the police station discovered this. They seized a roll of flower gambling paper, 33 rifle bullets, two opium pipes, one opium lamp, gambling money amounting to eight silver dollars, twelve dimes, and 1,950 copper coins, as well as opium dross and paste. The gambling bosses, Gao Genxiang and his wife Gao Zhu, were taken to the station. After interrogation by Chief Yao, it was determined that the case involved the opening of a flower gambling den, the private possession of firearms, and the violation of opium prohibition, all serious offenses. A document was immediately prepared and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation and handling.

Sentenced to Three Months Imprisonment

Fined Six Hundred Yuan

Ma Yisun, the accountant of the Yingfengyu Coal Company at number 116, North Henan Road, from Zhenjiang, is addicted to gambling. He goes to the roulette gambling den almost every day and loses almost every day. He embezzled funds from the company, accumulating a total of over 13,000 yuan. This was discovered by the company owner, Wu Suzhou, who reported it to the police, who arrested Ma. The day before yesterday, he was sent to the Special District Local Court. Upon hearing the news, Ma's family tried to repay the money. Winter Defense Patrol Duty on the Railway 157

Off-Duty Police Officers Not Allowed to Leave Without Permission

The General Section of Police Affairs of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways yesterday issued an order to all sections, stating that with the approach of winter defense and the imminent New Year, all trains and stations on the two railways are places where petty thieves seek to take advantage of. Therefore, prevention must be thorough. According to the order of the bureau, the winter defense measures were discussed at a meeting on November 22nd, attended by the chiefs of police affairs from all sections of the two railways. It was decided that the winter defense would start on December 1st of this year and end on March 1st of next year. Following the example of the special military curfew period, extra shifts will be added, with strict patrols day and night. All off-duty police officers, whether day or night, are not allowed to leave without permission to be available for temporary extra shifts. Police chiefs of all sections must supervise the station chiefs and police officers to connect with the stationed military police and pay close attention to strengthening strict prevention to protect travelers and maintain public security without any negligence that would lead to severe reprimands. This is the order.

Losses Amount to Three to Four Thousand Taels

Letter to the Editor 161

To the Editors of Shenbao:

Regarding the news report in your esteemed newspaper about the assassination of Mr. Wang Baoxie, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Rickshaw Guild, which mentioned that Mr. Wang had dealings with our guild and that the municipal government had ordered the suspension of licenses for the Hua-area rickshaw industry, we are deeply shocked. Mr. Wang is from the Zhabei rickshaw industry and the business scope of our guild, which is located in the Public Concession, is separate and has never had any relationship with our guild. Therefore, there is no question of many dealings. Furthermore, it is not true that the municipal government has recently ordered the Chinese and foreign rickshaw guilds in the concessions to join the Shanghai Rickshaw Guild before April 1st of next year to ensure uniformity, otherwise, licenses in the Chinese area will not be issued. Apart from the two notices we received from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau on October 7th and 15th to discuss our guild's joining the Shanghai Rickshaw Guild, we have not received any notice from any municipal government agency to suspend the issuance of licenses in the Chinese area. This matter concerns the reputation and interests of our guild members, so we hereby request a correction.

Respectfully,

The Chinese and Foreign Rickshaw Merchants Guild

December 21, 1919
